seen, flying the light because she had done evil, whereupon he wrote this
letter following.

Philotimus to his dearest Aurelia.
WOe worth ye man whose wealth consists in wishing, cursed be ye wretch who
knows not what to wish him: the one wastes his wind, and rowls a restles stone,
ye other spe^ds his sprites, and quenches thirst with tears. But if my
chance be both, as both God knows it is, then let all mortal wightes resign
to me their sighs, and damned souls in Hell, rejoice to have escaped my
snares. And why I do complain, give ear, and say your mind. I beard of late
a tale, too late, and yet too soon, of falshooode in Aurelia, and Treason to
Philotimus. Wherein I quickly wished, and yet I knew not which to wish, that ye
broker of it had either been dum, or I the hearer had happily been deaf.

Is it true Aurelia, that you are revolted, whose constancy hitherto Brute it
self has blushed to blame? Or is it false Aurelia, you have reuersed your
judgment, to deface flying Fame with your steadfast faith? The fame is spread,
that you are sped, and chaungd your pasture for better commons: my mistrust is
grounded upon love, and may be coniectured by probable surmises.

It was my will of late to visit thy lodging, where I found ye shrine but not my
Saint: the next day after I came again, and knocked at the gates till my
knockolls were sore, but none would open: yet thinking that gains would
recompense pains in time convenient (not unlike Baalls priests, that thought
to wake ye stock Baal with incessant crying) no long space after I came
again, and then my mistress was a sleeping.

If our long acquaintance, the trial of my service, the oath taken between us
to confirm our contract, cannot move you, yet my sweet Aurelia, let thy
plighted faith by chaste Diana, thy covenant sealed in presence of Juno, thy
vengeance denounced to ye breakers of faith, even by thine own words to the
great God Jupiter, defend the from perjury, the greatest impiety, that may
be committed

What is the action thou commencest against me, except too great love? Or
wherein did I ever offend thy person, except with straining my golden string,
I have stretched it so far till all is broken? My strongest accusation is a
brainsicke prodigality, my greatest discredit a few foolish debtes: The one
too true an Argument of a good mind, the other a common sickness which in time
may be recured.

My matching with you shall recover some credit, and your endowment shall
stop their mouths. I know how honorably they think of Aurelia, and when I
have something they will grant me respite, hoping that the interest of my good
husbandry in time will be able to disburse their discharge.

The Bird which finds her nest despoiled of her young ones, often lets her food
down fall, much like my self, which frustrate of thy presence am much
appauld? O Aurelia, if thine ear be tied to every lying tongue, which wisdom
forbids, or you should give me over in the plain feilde, which thine honor
denies, what a blemishe would it be to the brute of thy lignage, or to whom
might I address my grievous complaints, thou attainted of Treason, but I a
captive catiffe. If it be known that I am defrauded of thee by false
suborning wretches, and then to have nothing, every one will be snatching glad
to get any thing, and so bring me to worse then naught.

If thy wealth be great, it is a gift worthy such a giver, if it be little, it
may be made more with thy sparinge at home, which is rightly called the
greatest tribute, and shall be increased with my labor abroad, which shall be
so much the more, by how much ye less my substance is slender.

For Gods sake Aurelia, pardon my bluntnes in misdoubting thy loyalty, and
blame flying tongues which breed thy dishonor, and my unrest, and never
hereafter let them be of thy court, which are meeter to be counselors at the
market Cross. Let us either confer in speech wherein I will detect the
slanderous reports that have gone of thee, or at the worst fall meetinge in
mind, send me thine answer for a sure testimony of thy certeintie, which
shall be as welcome to me, as I was bold with you.

Your servant Philotimus was, is, and will.


Aurelia to Philotimus, that was once her servant, and is she hopes her friend,
sends greting.
Would destiny yield to pity (my good Philotime) or ability counteruaile
hartles sorrow, thy griefs might be relieved, which I cannot but lament, our
loves might continue, which necessity dissolues. But friezing cold adawes
the frying heat, weak croned eld benumms youths lusty lims. The pereles
beauty of None such Niceus in time is invested in Thirsites deformity, and
every thing is turned by time. Gold wasted, yet what so solid, credit
defaced, yet what more glorious, friendship forgotten, yet nothing so firm,
thus eueri tide does eb in time. Then curse we our chances, that we cannot
cure our losses, time beckes, and fortune bendes, and every surfeit forerunnes
a fast. Fortune has her fits of frowninges, endure them Philotime, if she
bring better, we are sweetly deceived, now force perforce mixeth honey with gall.

As hard it is for faithful Philotimus, to doubt of sincerity in Aureliaes
love, as uneasy for me to moderate affection, without unspeakable torments to
my loyal breast. Yet must I turn my Tippet ere I burn my bones, and lack
inlooked for love to cloy thy gulping gluttony, ere I cast my self away with
bootles attempts, and ad heaps of woes to our joint decay. The undoubted
certificate of thy long known feruencie, does give me a warrantize to term
thee my friend, and may give thee a caveat to prove thy self trusty, not
seekinge thy preservative with poisoning of me.

If I should give thee my poor portion, too bad to be boughte, and too much to
be begd, and solemnize our childish unadvised contract with a sond celebration
of weddinge, perchance thou had a servant to dance attendaunce (as the
Gods had wretched Vulcane to minister at their Table) but the smallnes of your
profit which scarce would be any, would quaise the force of pleasure and sauce
it with despite.

Nay Philotimus, had Medea suspected that before, which too late experience
taught her, that Iasons voyage had been undertaken for the lucre of goods,
not the love of her goodwill, he had hopte shorter, and she had sped better,
and Euripides had wanted some matter subject, to underprop his bloody style
upon the mounting Stages. Perseus brought Andromeda from the black Indians, I
wis with small wealth. And what had the Trojan for his Graekish rape? I wis for
wealth both war and woe. The worst sort of men, says Terence his Charinus, be
those, which get their profit by others disprofit, and gorge their extorcion by
poor men's windefalls. Scylla and Caesar both are noted for Landpyrates, for
robbinge Peter to pay Paul, filchinge from others to feed their friends, a
very part of the essence of coosining prodigality.

Did thou never read the properties of the pretty Merlin, who holding the
Lark all night between her little talantes to keep her warm, as soon as it is
morning vnfastens her hold, and lettes her fly, and marking which way she
takes her flighte, will not all the day following set winge to that corner? But
have thou not heard of the crooked natured Trochilus, who breeding in ye mouth
of Crocodilus, where he is nourished, becomes afterward as they say, the
Crocodiles Physician, I mean Philotimus, utterly kills him. The former of
these do all men commend, but the latter they most abominably detest.

Alas Philotimus, by what reason should thy eating of grapes, set my teeth on
edge, or when thou have spent thine own stock, seek a new booty with praing
on mine?

The gleade and the Dove do not match together, the Lion and the Lamb are not
coupled together, equality must be in marriage, or else it is not conuenable:
the year is apportioned into even parcells, Justice her ballaunce is of equal
peize, and the heavens are moved with an uniform equality, ye ship does whelm
or sink if either side be ouerweied, the right Democritia has no difference
of persons, and the virtuous mean is equally placed betwixt both extremes.
The^ Philotimus, since thou art a Gentleman by style, but a beggar by
misfortune, and I a poor Gentlewoma^ yet of so^e living, accuse me not of
perjury, wherein I am sackles, but blame thy mishap, whereof thou art causer.

I pray you be content to foster your Cuckoes birds at home, and carry them
not as the Cuckoes use, to an other birds nest, to bring forth. Content your
self with your own lot. It is vain for the Dutchman to wish himself an
Englishman, or the Thracian an Athenian.

Thou that displeasest thy self, how can thou please me? Indeed Jupiter and
Juno, Venus and Diana, were called to witness to my oath, and you had both word
and oath, and all but heart. Yet the vniuersallest Axioms have their cautions,
every Obligation has his condition, and this I added in mine oath, if you
were no chaungling: which condition being broken, I will not envy thee as an
enemy, yet must mind as I find without any faining.

Juno I hope will dispense with mine oath of love: for she was ever an enemy to
Venus.

Venus I doubt not, will be entreated to forgo the company of sorry wowers,
for she is painted of the Poets ever laughing, as one that loves no mourning.

Diana I dare say, will not be angry for forsaking sorrow, for she does
nothing but hunt and sport, and in her meriments falls in love with Endymion.

Jupiter I am sure, will not think that I have offended, for Homer calls him
Anculopetis, for speaking one thing, and thinking an other.

Not much unlike a child that having hurt himself with falling, must have an
other bett that never came nere him: so you by your reckles merit losing my
love, accuse an other of falsehood in fellowship, you neither know whom, nor
wherefore. This is worse then war knave quoth Tomkins to his shadow: for he
seeing his shadow in the night, took it for one that came to spoil him, to
whom, knauing it, and slauing it, he gave many a good bang: but you not yet
having learned the first point of hauking to hold fast, bitterly rail you
know not on whom, and shall have amends I cannot tell when.

You bring store of reasons to inueigle me with subtelty, whereof I will not
deny the effectual force, but opposing to them my continency, I will cross
me from such blessings. For as he is more continent, that amid the daintiest
banquet can use his abstinence, then he that refraines because he wantes: so if
I can shun thy seducing reasons, I shall think my self more temperate, the^
if thou had showen no reason at all, and I forborne thy company. For
every of thy reasons I have an hundred affections. Therefore desiste
Philotimus, and spurn no more against the prick.

Orion for offering to defloure Phaebe was slain by a scorpion. Thou art as
insatiable in thy kind, as Arist. philoxenus, yt wished himself a neck as
long as a Crane, to have his meat long a swallowing.

He that has served ten years in war, by the law of Arms may be priuildged
from all service. And since thou have played the amorous knight so long and so
truly, I am now content to give thee a discharge.

An Italian Soldiour in Charles the fifth his camp, having past many offices of
credit in Arms, was challenged of a young Gentleman, a nouice, scarce of two
years practice, to whom he made this awnswere. When thou haste trod the
impression of every my steps, and stied to the seat of my dignity, and
have combatted with all my perils, I will meet thee in the feilds, otherwise
I will not so much embase my self, which is as if a Nobleman should fight with a
ruffia^: so Philotimus, when thou have redeemed thy morgaged lands, and for
thy living may say to me, well overtaken, I will match with thee, and not
before.

Yet trust me Philotimus, feign would I help, but alas I may not. Thy
incrementes will be my detriments, and thy consumption now is almost past
remedy. Cynthia could not call her son Hyppolitus out of Hell, nor Theseus his
friend Perithous, nor Aurelia heal her cureles friend. I have not Venus her
skill, that made Phaon of an old man a yongman, nor thou art not a Bacchus to
be twice borne, once of his mother, and once of Jupiters thygh.

If I might have Alcests luck, that dying for her husband Admetus was restored
to life by Proserpina, I would show thee favor for so little harm. Yet my
good Philotimus, caskes will ever taste of their first licour, and I shall never
forget our old friendship. And therefore as Antoninus pius when he could not
help the poor widows son that was condemned to die, wept with her to bear
some of her grief: so though I can do thee no such good as thou look for,
I cannot but jointly wail thy woes.

Your friend as she may Aurelia.


As the fire, the more it is blown the brighter it flames: so he with
disperpled locks, and hair discheueled about his shoulders, set fire to his
desire, with an incessant meditation on his almost irrecuperable mistress,
wherewith he answered as follows.

Philotimus sends health, which he has not, to Aurelia his mistress, and
wishes her the mercy she should have toward her servant.
THE skillful that behold the picture of Aesculapius, commend not the picture,
but the painter, we extol not so much the taste of our meat, as the Cooks
cunning that seasoned it, no man estemeth his coin for the stamp, but for ye
right metal when it comes to the touch: neither do I Aurelia, like thine
aunsweres, but commend thy wit from whence they came.

You say you cannot boot me, yet do stumps of old love stick in your stomach.
Indeed well I know, that an hand chafed with flowers will after smell of them,
when they are gone, and that some cycatrice of ancient benevolence will
remain, when love it self is perished and maimed. Whereby it will fare with
me, as it did with Democritus, who goinge about for sorrow of his sisters
mishap to famishe himselfe^, was relieved three days with the smell of new
bread: Or as with the Philosopher whom Oribazius says in his time he knew
to live awhile by the sent of honey: and I shall live by the shadow of thine
old love, the substance whereof is as good meat for ghostes, as may be.

O Aurelia, what equity is this, to inchaunte me with thy Angelicke glaunces,
and now to deprive me of thy presence?

I may welll compare thee to the lake of Bytamin, whereof me^ that pass that
way, dare not venture the vewe, much less aproch the smell, except Eunuchs
that be gelded, which fear not to behold, neither are indaungered by the
smell: And he that gloates on thee, except such as feign would and cannot (as
Pythias says in Terence) may chance either wish his eyes were out, or that he
had fewer stones by one and an other.

For as at the great earthquake in Antioch, there escaped none saving one woman
and a slave) that was not hurt or deadlye wounded: so there be few beholders
of you, that lose not their liberty, except it be restored by your
liberality. But as the pillar which Traian the Emperor erected in the place
named Datia, of wonderful height and breadth all of one stone, was more
admirable to men, and did more enoble his person, then if he had composed it of
diverse stones: so you making and taking me your only mate without ever
chopping and changing to any other, shall perpetuate the peace of your mind,
and win commendation of unstained constancy.

Now to the canuasse of thy letters, whom I surueyed diligently without
delighte, and will answer speedily without despair.

Could it not suffice Achilles to slay Hector, but to dragge and hayle his
body through the duste? Was it not sufficient for Anthony to loppe Tullye by
the neck, unless Anthonyes wife did mangle his body, and wear his Tongue in
her hatte, to work his greater obloquie? Was it not enough for thee to untie
our true loves knot with the breach of truce, but to kill me again with
opprobrious words, Si modo qui periit, bis periisse potest? Your learning I
know more then your honestye, and that makes me speak Lattin to cover your
dishonestie.

Is it thine, not thee, thy gains not goodwill, that I do wowe? Lie not
Aurelia, when thou know the truth. It is a great shame, and a greater
sin, and almost coossen to that pleadelesse fault that cannot be forgiven,
either here or else where. No Aurelia, it is mine hosts not mine Inn yt I am
a guest for. It is the flock not their wool, for whose cause I so sadly sit
whuppinge all the day under a hill. Indeed lucre is a lure to much
dissembling. But though I am needy, yet am I not greedy, but well sufficed
with a small sise of wealth, and my minds music were well in tune, if thou
would but add one string of thy consent. The relation of my misery to the
mystery of your wealth, was to persuade you not to shrink in the wetting, but
like a Kentish cloth that stains with nothing, stand inuiolated.

Cupid is blind, and sees no riches. Lycurgus the Lawgiver of the
Lacedaemonians, commanded those of his City, that they should offer to the
Gods, few things in number, and not rich in value. In the law which God gave
unto the Hebrews, he was so limited in the things he demanded, and so
human in ye things he commanded, that in order of the sacrifices which they
should offer, he did ordeine that the poor man which could not offer a
goat, should offer no more but of the hair thereof. The consideration of
these gave me hardines to embolden my courage in this amorous encounter, though
I have no pay to counteruaile ye semblaunce of a Captain: the same efficacy
may humiliate you, for want of better Harvest, to take oats in part of
payment.

Paulus Aemilius vanquishing Perses King of Macedonia, rather desired honor
then a quarrie of treasure. Anthonio offering to die before the Emperor that
sought his death, was received into former grace. Though I were Iris or
Codrus, and thou in potencie might match with Rome, in riches with Tyrus, in
beauty with Helia, in opulence with Tarence, yet the repulse of my love
without remorse, will show thee more cruel then all the beasts in the
deserts of Africa, or those of ye great India. India. A wayfaring pilgrim
taking a thorn out of a Lions foot, meetinge after with him at the games of
Olympia, and being brought out to wrestle with him would not use his furious
force but with a grateful recordance acknowledging his curtesy fawned upon
him. It greues me to exhort thee to square thy imitation to a beasts
clemency: then let thy courtesy be a ready remedy to make me ashamed of my
unequal comparison. As Telephus had nothing to cure his hurt, but the launcing
of the spear that gave him his wou^d, and as the mind is conceived with
nothing but the mind: so nothing can counteruaile the value of love, but an
aunswerable conformation of the desired love.

For which cause, poor unbegotten wether beaten Qualto, an hobhansom man god
wot, and a bow wow to his Lady and mistrisse, serving a Lady in Italy as a Tom
drudge of the pudding house, or a groom to her close stool, or a seruitour to
such slavery, asking on a time after the disclosure of his loyalty, some
guerdon requitable in lieu of all his pining thoughts to win her affections,
and pinching pains about her drudgerie, she was content to imbezle some part
of her goods to notifye her larges toward Qualto. But this, nor any thing
could enforce him to relinquish his suite, saving the yelding of her battered
breast. Wherefore never giving over (which Ovid commaundes us in his Art of
loving) as small drops in time pearce the hard marble: so he with urgent
instaunce in his attempted enterprise, got her in arms that had his heart in
hold, and like a valiaunte waterman setting his ores, was permitted to row in
his mistress boat.

But my love thou know is noe weed for wantons wear, no fancies freake
with knackinge fetches, not like a bow long bent yt in process weakens, but
like ye natural motion of an eleme^t which in going gathers strength. Thou
telst me of Orion, who for offering to defloure Diana, was killed by a Serpent:
wherein thou imitates the Devil in his alleging of Scriptures, for he never
bringes out an whole text, but so much as is for his own enorm intended
purpose: and thou take the half serving thee, and leaves out the moitie
making for me, that utterly overthrows thy whole province. For though Orion
were bereaved of this tra^sitorie life, yet that which is more glorious, he
was by imputed elevation translated into a star.

If as Rams retire to strike harder, so your love recule to return with more
vehemency, I shall think, that as ye best vines in Germany grow on hard
rocks, so the surest love inhabites the heart hardliest attoned: and as the
praise of a Judge is not given to his scarlet gown, so your good liking is not
framed by your lookinge. Then shall I curse the Eclipse of my waininge
Judgment, that of late have judged your demeanor measured by your favor, an
apishe deformity in clothe of Goulde, and your ill manner, scarce agreeable to
so great a Lady.

Phoebus I know does not always harp, sometime he shoots, Triacle does not
ever cure, sometimes it poisoneth, and friends must not ever love, but by
intermission, sometimes mislike. Iars of necessity must be among friends, but
thrice woe be to them by whom they come.

Ah Aurelia, feign would I singe, but fury makes me fret, and rage has sworn
to seek revenge of wrong. In dread and danger would I pass between the
stringe and bow, to have my will on that birds bushed cage, that does incense
my care. O that I might have a shoot at one of the Deares in his Park, if yt
were but his Heart, Aurelia, it would suffice me.

I know there be vnderminig easinge droppers, that have wroughte this
estraungment between us. But since the Myll will needs about, the pin
whereon the Mill does go, I will assay to strike it out, and so the Myllne to
overthrow.

The mind I have is of gold to serve thee, but of iron to break their pride,
and if I want armor wherewith to fight, I want not a mind to abide death.

Thus thou see Aurelia, I am not like the stripling Pertinax, who used to
sell his wood so dear, contentious, and pinching, yt if they gave him not his
first demand, did rather leave his wood vnsould, then abate one blancke of his
price. For though I suffer a sower repulse, yet am I content to awaite thy
leisure.

Your most faithful servaunt Philotimus.


Aurelia at the receipte of these letters, was moved wish a marvelous disdain
of Philotimus, who durst be so boulde as threaten her new friend, his letters
she answered in these words.

I Cannot tell Philotimus, whether thou art better to keep an hold, or to play
a prating beggar. For thou and thy purpose stick together like burres, neither
though forbid, wilt ever leave of thy iangling. Thy commendation of my wit
enhaunceth no pride. For the Satyrs thought poor Martia to surpass in
music, Coridon preferred his oten pipe, before Apolloes silver Harp, and
Poliphem the blind Giaunt, thought sielie Galataea to excede the beauty of
Mars his concubine.

Good simple soul, would you pick a quarrel with them, that as you say,
would pick a thank with me? Alas pretty figboy, an hasill twigge in your
hand, is an whole haulbarde.

Thou art better to be a gunner under a Ladies targett, then Lieutenaunt of a
pitched field. Indeed? And is your barking tongue turned to biting teeth? you
are now fleshed in impudency. If you be chafed you shall be walked, if you be
hot you may be cooled. A young colt plungeth at the first prick, as though he
felt no ground, but being chafed a little, champes on his bridle and stands
still.

The more a sore is rubbed and handeled, the less it heales: the more busy you
are to be a stickler in your own cause, yt further aloof am I of: you cannot
shift your cards so cleanly but you ar seen. Do not tell me, yt I am a
whetstone to set every dainty tooth on edge, and so clawe an Ass till you
have rid her.

Physicians use a contrary plaster to those patientes, that will not heal
with the rules of physic, and I must handle you roughly, whe^n fair words
cannot serve to make a fool feign.

But this I cannot forget, how full of guts you are, at one blow to kill God
have mercy on his soul. You may if you will, but do if you dare. Alas good
Philotime, thy force of arms be no force, no harm. Thou art comd of a gentle
kind, to gave so wide and not to bite. Indeed you are all heart but head, and
that is horns, but if you be lusty, you may go louze you. Me thinks when I
hear thee tell of thy valor, I see ridiculous Bacchus, whom Aristophanes in
Canis brings in drunken, marching in Hercules his armor, and saying he would
go down to see the Tragedies in Hell.

Nay holla squaring Dick, I am no but for every boult. Thou do but chase a
shadow in the sun when thou followest me. Though thou sweat blood, as the
Bird Eradius does in the time of treading, it will sooner bring thee to a
bloody flixe, then to my favor. I am not so blind, that thou can make me
believe with a wink, it is midnight at noone day. The bird Osprey is of such
whitenes on his breast, that houering over the fishpoole, all ye fish turn up
their bellies, and so he takes his pray. Keep thy fair promises in thy purse,
for with me they little prevail, and less persuade.

When the Lion is old, all the beasts of the feilde condemn him, and as you
are too old a friend to be good, so your heirs be of age to take your place,
expecting your resignation.

Thou art like the Apes called Callitrices, which at the new of the moon
rejoice, and at the full and waining be triste and sad. You in the beginning of
our love were very iocunde, and at our diuorcement use your terms of
railing. But though the Dragon cannot abide the Panther, yet all other beasts
resort to behold his colors, and smell of his odor, and though the Batte hate
the light, yet is the light nothing the worse.

When the Eagle has two or three birds, she castes out one of them, fearing
her self not to be able to nourish them, whom the Bird Ossifraga receives
and brings up, as though it were her own. Aeneas lost Libye, yet he found
Latium. Traian could not live with Domitian the Emperor, yet flyinge to Nola
in Campania, he found Plutarch for his master, Plotina for his wife, and Nerua
for his father, who afterward being Emperor, adopted Traian to be his son.
Comfort thy self, there be more maids then Maukin and though thou lose me,
thou may find some other. Coridon shall be loved else where, though fond
Alexis do disdain.

The serpent cannot blame the Heart though he be his enemy, and his bane,
because it is natures ordinance: neither may the Raven rightly accuse the
little bird Easalon for breaking of her eggs, because their discord is sown
of nature. Neither can the Swan look for friendship of the Eagle, yet neither
of both to be discommended. The fishes Muges abound above measure in love
toward their own kind and sort, and list not meddle with the fellowship of
others. Minerua turned the hairs of Medusa who^ she hated into adders, yet who
does obiecte it to Minerua for cruelty?

Have thou not heard of the foolish marriage that the Emperor Heliogabalus
made betwixt the image of the Goddess Pallas and the God Heliogabalus, which
being consummated to the great laughter of his enemies, and the grief of the
Romans to see their Gods defaced, he made them likewise a bed in the midst
of the Temple, where they might sleep together? Under as small guard and
veneration shall our marriage stand, and as little joy I fear, should we feel
yfere, as did the two insensible pictures.

If thou think thy interest be better in me, because thou have been at
some cost on me, this I say, yt I never meant to prove my self a noddy with
refusing offered gold, neither am I of such power as the Popes holiness, to give
a pardon of thy sins, for a few Peter Pence. Certain men brought from
Graece to Rome a false will of one Lucius Manutius Basilius, a rich man, the
legacies whereof that they might more easelye compass, they writ in with them
two Noble men of Rome, M. Crassus, and Q. Hortensius both expert civil
Lawiers, and eloquente Orators. These two Gentlemen, although they suspected
it to be forged, yet notwithstanding knowing themselves giltles of all faults
in the devise, were well enough content to be parceners of his lands.

It is the law of arms in many places, that he which is first in the
skirmish, though he submit himself, yet being taken, shall be wounded for his
offense. Then neither think me tirannous for giving you the glieke, though you
were my first friend, neither imagine your fortune adverse, neither vex your
self with impacable sorrow. That flower must not grow, that can abide no cold:
you may not warm you by a fire, but you must feel the flame: he that has his
beard most curiously washed in the Barbers shop, will take no snuff to have it
cast out into ye open streets.

But since sielie manling, thou art so obstinate in straining the fault to
inexorable Aurelia, I will give thee a specialtie what guard I have of thee, in
showing thee an electuary against thy love, which thou being a student ought
to know better then I, yet art so busy in bootles business, going about to
get a Cock with egg, that thou can not or wilt not see wood for trees.
Read Cadmus the Milesian, who has written a whole book in the remedies of
love, and that Ovid which has infected thee with his lasciuiousnes, has given
thee a mean to clawe of his itche.

The beast Fiber perceiving himself to be pursued of the hunter, biteth of his
stones, which are merueilous good in medicines, and lays them in the sight of
the hunter, knowing by nature yt he is hunted for the same: so (Philotimus) I
can yield, if thou want money, and a little may pleasure thee, to let thee
have of my small store, knowing very well (saving ye reverence of your
protestation (that it is the coin, and not the woman you seek after. Or I
will deal with thee, as a noble man of Rome sometime did with his ancient
manor house. This noble man behoulding the follies of Commodus then Emperor,
the tyrannies of Pere^nius vicegerent of the Empire, and the spoils of the
commonwealth, he both sincere in judgment, and severe in life, departed from
thence to the country of Liguria, to live in a poor village, where sometimes
his father had made his habitacle, and buying that poor cottage, built in ye
compass thereof a stately building, permitting the old to remain in the midst,
without addition or diminution thereof: and since I must needs condescend to
your importunate entreatie, you shall have the title of mine old friend now
ruinous, as one of who^ I have ere while smackt the relish of reposed rest,
marry an other platform I have laid, whereon I purpose to erect an edefice of
some more stately frenship, in whose breasts I mean to situate my mantion house.

It is not for me Philotimus, to deal with him that can card more in one
night, then I and many a good huswife can spin all the day. Martia, Letus, and
Electus, killing Commodus on the night, commanding certain slaves to bestow
his body at their appointmen, wrapped in an old seron, wherein the ordure of the
stable was wont to be carried out, chose an other before day, to the end the
Empire might have an owner, and they have defense under his protection: and
since I have forlorn thee, blame me not though I have elected an other for
mine own safeguard: farewell Philotimus, and be answered with reason.

Aurelia your old friend.


Philotimus reading these letters, was nothing appaulde, but with confidence
of recovery, answered as follows.

THe Leopard pursues his pray leaping and startling, and if he take it not the
third or fourth leap, he stinteth for indignation, and goes backwarde as
though he were overcome.

When the Elephants of king Porus, were a little wounded by ye soldiers of the
great Alexander with their weapons called Capidae, and were put in fear they
were more hurtefull to their own rulers, and casting them down and tearing the^
in pieces, ran out of the battle like sheep. But I neither mean to be as
short as ye Leopard in his hasty huntinges, nor so cowardly as ye Elephant in
his attempted assaults. And yet I cannot but yield to you, and pray to your
pleasure for a comfortable remorse. The gray mare is ye better horse,
especially if she be a curtal, it must be as ye woman will, when all is said
and done. Though Mars were the God and Bellona but a Goddess, yet she had the
pre-eminence in all martial attemptes.

But would any man have judged you a backeslider, so soon to have turned your
tongue to your tail, and for continuing of your sensual pleasure, to have
flitted from an old friend to a new flatterer? As none rould heal Philoctetes
poisoned feet, but Machaon, Aesculapius his son: so you labor of a disease,
that none can heal, but he that will pay for lending of his patiente. It is
not my purginge pills (which, you say, would poule you of all your coin)
but Cornelius his sweet suppositorye, that must minister you physic.

It grieves me less Aurelia, that you have given me over, then that mine
innocence being known, as shortly it will, you shall be noted of lightenes
and lewdenes. Whereby it will come to pass, that as the name of Iulia among
the Romans, was an ensign of a common adultresse strumpet: so the name of
Aurelia for thy sake, henceforward shall be detested as a note of frail
inconstancy.

Ay me but cast away, Ah dear Aurelia, my power is too weak to make any
war, and yet I can find no peace, I am not scorcht with any fire, and yet no
cold adawes my heat: I cannot die as ye happy dye, to ye end to live for
ever, but I must live, as misers live, to the end to die for ever.

O that every hair of my head were a man for his adherentes sake, who is no
good curre, for that he bites behind, much less a whelpe of the princely
Lion, who being chased with hounds or hunters, seeks no couerte wherein to
lurk, but sits in the field where he may be seen, and araieth himself to
battle. I do not level by guess (as thou do burden me) at him, that does
this villainy, but know him, and can name him, in this resembling the Lion,
who being vulned, takes such heed, that he knows who first smote him, and
rises on the smiter, though he be in never so great a multitude. If there be
any poison prepared in an house, a partridge pende up in a cage or coupe, will
byte and scratch, and cry out, such Divination has she by nature, and such
have I by Gods predestination to descry mine enemies trains.

Yet take you heed you lean not to hard on a broken staff. It may be, it is
for small goodwill to thee, but for envy to me, yt he busieth himself: much
like the Griphon in the Hypeborian hills, where being bred plenty of gold and
precious stones, as ye Smaragde, the Jasper, the Crystal, neither has he use
of the^ him self, neither suffers them to be taken from thence, as diverse good
writers affirm: or the Cameleon, who drawing to the goshaukes, against whom his
most might stands, they also fly unto him, and by this means he takes them,
wilfully to be devoured to other beasts. But as the Linx perceiving that his
urine does turn in to a precious stone named Ligurius, and naturally enuyinge
yt should be any use to mankind, hides it wiih sand or earth, when he has
pissed, which is ye very cause yt it sooner hardens, and turns into a
stone: So I do not doubt, ^ut this labor to put me out of conceit, may in
time after trial of my faith and his falsehood, convert to my greater grace
with thee, and credit with others

You after your scoffing manner put me in the predicament of the Apes
Callitrices. Yet those that laugh at me, for triumphing before the victory,
and reckoning my shot before mine hostess, and thinking I had thy heart before
I searched thy reins, may deem thee a light huswife for thy cracked
fidelity. It is no maisterie to deride one in misery, but it is convenient to
banne the causers of it. Thy untoothsome tauntes may well compare thee to the
sorcering Sirens, who are merry in tempests, and heavy in fair weather.

If it be the destiny of him that first wooes you, to be forlorn, as it was
prophesied that he which first stepped on the Trojan ground, among the
Grecian host, of neceessitie should be slain, which was verified in
Protesilaus (though he might vaunte that he was slain by Hector, and I repine
to be undone by a coward) Or if as the monster Sphynx slew all that passed by
her to the city of Thebs, if they could not expound her riddle, so you will be
the bale of all that cannot display your sleightes: It may fall out that as
Laodamia wastfullie mourned for her Protesilaus, or as when Oedipus had given
Sphynx a solution, she brake her neck for grief: so thou may wish ere
thou dyest for poor Philotimus, and when thy cautele fetches shall be laid open,
follow Phillis in the end, though far unlike her in thy life.

Now then recule with reconciled grace (my Alderlieuest Aurelia) a name unto my
soul as sweet as balm. The shield of love, the force of faith, that trusty
targe, has long borne of, and broke the thrustes that malice at me throws.
Mine only shield has long forwarded a sorry man, now quickly lend me yours,
or else you do me wrong. Still are you bound by faith, though fancy would
be free, still are you fast by oath, though loath to lau^e it out. En bon gre
take a pouer boy, for I am yet Philotimus. Ten thousand times a day desire
does live and dye, feign would I live to gain thy love, or die with grief to
leave with loss. If Desire thy darling be wayward, let thy yielding remorse
sing alullibie lullie, if I be in presumption a Giant to solicit my suite,
which am in power a gnat to perform any service, yet shall my deuoire do his
endeavor to gratify thy cu^rtesie, and work thy delighte: and know that
nettles and egshells are good for something, which being burnt together to
powder and put in your nose, will stau^ch the blood of wounds or nose. If thou
think for my craft I have a Foxes tongue, or that for my smart I am a thorn
in your foot, yet wot you, that a Foxes tongue laid to the sore in thy foot
or hand, will undoubtedly heal it.

Though in your conceit I am knauishly mannered, yet do thou imagine me
apishly witted, and if your fleetinge phantasye think me crabbedlie favored,
a foul ground for your fair cou^terfeit, you know, may well agree. When the
field is Argent, and that which occupies the field is Sable, that shield is
called fairest in field. Full often ye whitest Doves with speckled Culuers tread,
and often we see the Turtle brown with Popimay does wed. If you mislike my
droupinge pace, with my ragamuffin vesture, one good word of your goodwill, may
make me cast my lothsame sloth, and yet renew my lusty liuerie. The Bears
whelps lie blind in a confused lump, till their dear dams do lick them:
the best Pearls have no show, till the Lapidaries clear them: neither can
you use the best mettald knife, till the Cutler have glazd it.

Ambages laid aparte, if thou had a counterpane of my tyring languor, or how
as waxe^ torch with sulphur touched, I burn, I neither needed Gracchus his
poynaunt eloquence, at whose Oration the whole congregation wept: nor
Symonides his doleful skill, that invented the waymenting order of verses
termed Lyrici, and was excellent in procuring men to tears: nor to be expert
in the woeful Elegies, to move thee to pity a disconsolate wretch. Who can
give to me a fountain made of moan, that I may weep as much as is my will,
and fouse my sorrow up in swelling tears? O that I had her love in link, that
has my heart in hold. Then would she procure, the Sea seem calm, the
billows calm, the earth rejoice, the air to singe, no surge by Sea, no
smarte by land I should endure. Plisthenides, thou were yblest, what cares
soever did eucroch: For whether winds did toss thy bark, or surging seas
dismayed thy breast, ay thy wedlock went with thee, with clinching arms thou
her embrast. In this thou art happy (Aurelia) that thou can not see me, for
if thou could, you would die for woe, and most unhappy that thou will not
see me, for now thou shall live in ignomie.

Mine heir, whom thou say has outgrowen his minority, looking for his
fathers inheritance, will neither wish to feel the pursuit of the like pain,
by pattern of his pear, neither long to be enfeoffed in such lands. His
forefathers name is Love, his lands are Loss, a common hire for such an heir.

I am tedious in ye prolonging of my letters, and eftsoons in their
reiteration, because that as Paracelsus used to say, in every natural thing
there is as well fresh oil, as salt brimstone, which by art may be extracted:
so I hope that in thy flintie stomach there is not only an harbor of cruelty
and disdain, but some deal also of merciful courtesy, which by my diligence
may be derived to the behoof of my distres. In the hardest flint may be found
some live lie spark of fire, the knottiest piece of box may be wroughte to a
dudgen hafte, and Aristotle says, that out of the salt sea foam may fresh
water be sifted. Then may I hope, that as these apparaunt impossibilities do
naythelesse work these prefixed efficacies, so out of thy stonye heart, may
yet flow such water, as may wash and purge my yearnfull wounds. Think some
and some is honest play.

O let not (was) work all delight, let (is) and (shall) have part in pay:
command, and I will slay my self that yours may be ye guilt, but bately bid
me die, and I will die forthwith for joy, that never yet I showed my self
ungrateful to my mistress. Yet if you will not so, but keep me still alive in
vexed plighte, for some offense I have committed, then show in what, or where,
or when, I stumbled in my steps, when it was my part to go vprighte, and as
Sceuola when he erred in slaying Porsenna the cruel Tyraunte, and killed his
Steward for him by a mistake, thrust his hand that did the deed, into the fire
for a penalty, and there consumed it: so ye part or member that has offended
thee, shall to make restoration of my love, and satisfaction for my fault,
dearly abie his leasings. I can endite no more for tears, and it is no
doughtie manly deed to fend my self with tears. Thus then noe more by me,
for me, but to thy mercies I appeal.

Your trustiest servant Philotimus.


These letters were delivered by his page, who had much ado to get the return
of an answer. For Aurelia weary of his wooing, and loath to hear of her
dealing, and given all to her darling, could not spend one vacant hour out of
Cornelius his company, scarce to read his letters, much less to answer
them. But at ye boys impudent entreatie, she vouchsafed forsooth to write
these two lines ensuing.

Aurelia once again to Philotimus.
A Robe whereof many men must wear the liuereies, must be used sparingly, and
not all spent on one: And Aurelia that has more to serve then you, must not
trifle all her time in giving you attendaunce. When I red thy letters in the
presence of Cornelius, and made collation of thy qualities with collection of
his properties, only this I had to say. A puttocke set on pearche fast by a
Falcons side, will quickly show it self a Kite. If this construction be
applied to your stomach, it will be a good confectio^ to stint your shameless
love. Farewell. I warn you that I see no more of the bastardly brood of thy
letters, which have neither head nor foot, nor any good substance. Thy
reasons be so cold, that they have frozen my love.

Aurelia willing to be your friend, and urged to be your foe. Amor quo serior eo
verior solet esse.


Philotimus having red his mistress sharp censure, writ presently without
pausinge to his pretty paunce, not so sharply as she, but as swiftly as he
could.

IT is a custom of purloining burglairers, to strew pepper in the tract of
their steppings, that the blood hound snuffing it into his nosthrilles, shall
not be able to trace them: so to make me run counter, or give over the chase,
you cast me a fuming fancy, and a flaming freewill, which whiles I feed on,
the game is gone.

There is a Well in Illirica, into which if any thing be put to cool, or to
extinguishe, it smouldringly burns it to very cinders: There are found
certain stones in a river in Pontus, which the^ take on fire, when ye wind is
greatest, and by how much ye more they are covered in water, by so much the
fearcer and brighter they burn: and how it comes to pass I know not, but
the less hope I conceive of thy liking, the more I desire and crave thy love.
The wallnut tree well bet when his nuts are shaken, bears more fruit the
year ensuing: the more you strike iron upon the stidhy, the harder and tougher
ye iro^ is: It is ye nature of a wild Irish man, yt the worse you use him, the
more service he does you: such and so luckles am I in my cheuisaunee, which
having feendly food corsed for love, and being sourelie rebuked for fawning on
thee, am yet as fruitful in thy love, as the beaten wallnut tree, as toughe as
the iron to bear any blows, and as mad as the Irishman, to give love for
lothinges.

For though my wits be blunted and hoodwinked, ye panicle of my brain damped
and discrased, and my spirits surcharged with griefs visitation, yet is my
hope ancored on thy qualification, and stoutly indurate against misaduentures.

When thy prick me dainty Cornelius, shall be vacased of his vain vizarde,
and disburdened and disballassed of his hypocritical apparitions, then shall
my poor habit be anteposed his proud heart, and the simplest diet prove the
best Physic.

Aurelia, to elect me to the calling of thy most intimate friends, and
reject me to the number of thy greatest foes, were to call me to the roste, and
beat me with the spitte, to shoe my horse, and prick him in the quick. But
as the River Lycus swallowed up by gaping of the ground, a great way thence is
in an other channel found: and as the Brook Erasine among the feildes of
Arge, one while sinkes, an other while runs in ouerflowing measure: and
Amasane eke in Sycill land does sometime rise afloat, and sometime sloppeth up
his spring: so will thy faintinge love recover with new recourse, whose
pleasure is at this time to give thy Hawke tyringe, that hereafter he may be
stronger and sharper at his game.

An Ass lives by the course of nature 30. years, and a sheep but ten,
therefore I doubt not but that cowardly sheep, will be soon defeated of his
hope, as well as I sielie Ass was deceived of my trust.

It were hard dealing, if in payment of a good gub of Gold, of full weight and
poise, one poor piece somewhat clipped and lighter then his fellows, may not
be foisted in among the rest, and pass in pay for current coin. Good sweet,
be not saunce all pity, but let ye right of ready will my lite poor wealth
excuse. O how you cut me in calling me Kite, much like as the thunder cutteth
the tree. For as that pearceth the bulk, and never hurts the bark, so
though you grieve my heart, you hurt not my manners, but if you can cut me no
otherwise, your wits will rust for want of good usage, and that you should
cut in such a matter, you had need go set them to a grindstone. As all Women
be evils, yet necessary evils: so though the Kite be a vermin, yet is
she a very necessary vermin. The Kite can weed the worm, can kill the
Moulewarpe, can cleanse the streates, and saving the Hens poor progeny, none
can accuse him of fellonie.

As the snowie mulberie, that bore before white Lilly leaves, having her white
beires besprinckled with true lover Pyramus his blod, became all purple black:
even so thy fair etheria^hew be stained with the guilt of sackles blood, shall
loose ye the grace and favor.

The victor has his price, when he has run his, race and so let me. Precious
stons are tried to be true if they be rubbed with lead, and change not their
hew, for they never receive any other color: and gentlewomens loyalty is
then experimented, when neither want of wealth, nor any frown of fortune, can
work loves alienation. You say my letters have neither head nor foot: then in
deed I grant, they are none of my brood: for I am sure I have both, I feel
by the weight of my head, which you have set with horns, and by the pain in
my feet, which I have got with running after you.

Thus trusting that you will not take my liuerie from me, before it be half
worn, nor bereave me of love in his best prime, I commit you to the protection
of the great God Cupid, who I beseech, even to direct you in your doings, as he
rules and governs me and my heart: for my self, I pray nothing else but ye
God and Saint Aurelia give me their blessing.

Your Servant Philotimus, who wishes himself as able to be your friend, as he
is unwilling to be your foe. Better late then never.


Amor qui prior, eo potior debet esse.
When Aurelia se, that neither ye wile of fair words, nor yt revile of soul
writs, could intrept or let his letters, the^ as one reading a riddle, or
constring an Embleame, she stood in a mamering what mean to make, or how to
thwart ye cost to shu^ his gu^shot. In this deur both dau^geous and doubtful,
she meant not to dallye being brought to this baye, nor to delay judgment in
taking day, but in few words and those well thewed, to manacle his
melancholye and mue up his love: wherefore in an abreuiat compendius of this
speedy speech ensuing, she gave him a general acquittaunce for all his
queint conceits, that his Memoradums and bills of debtes should never after be
flapt in her mouth.

Aureliaes discharge to all the debenters of her coosninge freende Philotimus.
Fools and little Dogs, are Ladies play fellows: A sower sallet may long be
eaten without satietie: the conclusion these premises is, that I can once
again vouchsafe to make me sport with the nody Philotimus, and answer his
displeasaunt untoothsome letters.

Men used to drink the waters of the brook Anigrus heretofore, but after what
the Centaurs vanquished by her Hercules in fight, did therein wash their
wounds, it was abhorred: the well of horned Hammon is at midnight passing hot,
and at noonetide passing could: So could I have brooked thee before I see thy
good conditions stand on the condition of wealth, whom in the night, yt is in
thy scarcity I have found as hot as Hay haruist, who^ in the day, yt is, thy
prosperity, I have known as could as a Chrismas evening.

You say better late then never, and I answer, as good never as to late.
Surcease thy sighs and flattering freaks, they naught prevail. Bacchus in
licknes of a grape beguiled Erigone yt suffered rape. Neptune in a Dolphins
shape, enforced Melantho to her shame. Then eft I say, and often before have
wished, that thou leave these crouched vows and orisons, icrested with triple
treachery, for as lickelie is that which Didimus writes, that if one put wool
in his ears, sheep will follow him, as that a fair word wrought one Arts
forge, can seduce me to the sequence of your wish.

Though I envy thee now, thou should not vye it with malice. It used to be
the guise of religious hostyers, to drink wine their fill, and ^ate while they
listed, and to offer the residue in Sacrifice to their Gods, and to pick the
meat as nere as they could- and give the furbished bones in immolation. The
Grecians in, tending to gratulate Ajax for his brave encounter with Hector,
roasted a bull, and eat him up, and presented Ajax with horns and hide: no
worse then this will I deal with you.

Have thou never heard how Homer describe Strife, that though it be basely
borne yt is take original of a slender cause, yet ^esteth not til she touch the
heaven with her head, still keeping her feet below on the earth, and therefore
thou may surmise my hate to be hotter, and shall miss of thy purpose if thou
look for better.

It is wholesome for the, Philotimus, to wear horns. It is a-tried medicine
that if the right side of thy head do ache, a comb made of the right side of
a Rames horn, will help it, and if the left side ache a comb of the left
horn will cure that Megrim.

Thou praiest that God and Saint Aurelia will bless thee, I adioyne, such a
Saint God send thee-Disdaine not I say once again, that want makes me for sake
thee, for outward things have great force, look of what color you would have
your chickins be, paint it on the outside of the eggs and they will prove:
and if you will have Venus her love, you must maintain her outward bravery.

Celmus for clinging most faithfully to Jupiter, became an Adamant: but by my
troth (Philotimus) I never mean to incur the like displeasure, for being too
faithful to thee. For thou art neither sweet for smell, nor seemly for sight.

Thou ask if I do thee right, and I answer, noe, worong, short talk to
make, thy tyring lu^st no loytring lodge can find within my breast. A Circes,
as I am can set thy ship on sand, I utterly renounce both thee and thine from
henceforward for ever more, if thou seek to exulcerate thy supposed injury,
as thy gaul is greater then thy guile, so I hope thou will breast for very
malice, ere thou matchest me to do me harm: at one word farewell forty
pence, too dear of three shillings, I never mean to be at more cost with you.

Thy vowed enemy Aurelia.


As Soon as Philotimus had read these letters he waxed pale as any box, a
shuddering through him struck, even like the sea which suddenly with whissing
noise does move, when with a little blast of wind it is but touched, with
driueling and with vapoured eyes, and frying fearce with straingie glead, and
lyinge groufe upon his face he still exclamed upon Aurelia, he meynt his
weeping with his blood, where with in stead of brine they were embrued, in this
cureles ecstasy, he left himself one min nuts respite to send this Aurelia
fainting farewell.

EVen as the snowish swan does singe before she dye, upon Meanders winding
banks, that sheds his straglinge streams and shears the fruitles sand with
wrakfull waves, so singe I now not notes of joy but lays of deep lament. I
write not, for I think my words may ought prevail: For why? I know the
haughty Gods at this my purpose spite. But since my wealth, my corpse, my fame,
and spotles mind, are lost by canckred hap, to wast my words I recke it little
cost. New love remains for thee (but not a new Philotimus) with other troth to
be impaund, which thod again may break.

O now I see (Democritus) that vain were they, and most ridiculous, which
derided thee when thou soughtest for Truth in the bottom of a Well. For well
know thou, how Truth was disperaged immediately after the death of our
forefathers, and glad for the avoiding of Falsehoods sentinels, to seek some
little corner to shroud it self in.

And your assertion (O Laureat Poets) wherein you affirm, ye Mars the God of
Discord and sower of all Sedition, was borne of Juno without the company of
man, semes to me to bear no small palm. For no offense need be given to
incense them to ire, they are teastie by nature, and have disdain by heart,
without ye instruction of any Schoolemaister. The Bucke is enclosed in the
park, a bridle rules the horse, an hook catches the fish, the Woolfe may be
tied, the Tiger may be tamed, only this is veritable, a Woman is vntamable:
no spur can make her go, no bridle hold her back, no courser sit her,
finally she will never forget injury, nor give thanks for benfites.

Would God that it were constituted for a law in Italy, which was a custom
among the Brackmans, that every Woman which entertained more then one suter in
all her life, should have her body divided and distributed equally to all her
lovers, so should neither sielie suitors be lyrched of their due, nor Woomen so
often have cause to say, full seldom comes the better, they would not seek
further and fare worse, but stay at home and live in security. Yet for thy
sake (Aurelia) I had rather wail mine own want, then wish thee that harm,
and will rather pray for thy speedy repentance, then curse thy disloialtie
that has spilte all my speed.

Sir Meleager adventured to kill a monster for fair Atlantaes sake: but for
thy sake I wish, that either Venus had never been bredde, or that I and my
swath cloutes had been drowned in the billows of Cytharis, from whence she
and her ofspringe is derived.

On me ye swarth Em^es fling the flames you bear: On me (O Hecate) work thy
sorcering tirannies: on me try both your teenes, and for my sake yet spare that
wretch Aurelia.

Thou say (Aurelia) thou will never be at more cost with me. God knows,
thy cost was small, and thy courtesy is less, but though it be some pleasure
to unthankful wightes for to obiecte the good forepassed tournes, yet will I
pretermit to show how chargeable thy service has been to me, and dismiss
thee from such reckoninges. Ah Aurelia, farewell for ever: and I pray God give
thee better speed then thou deseruest, and no worse then I wish thee.

By thine and Fortunes prisoner, Philotimus.


He received no answer of these his letters, neither did he look for any,
but restles flung up and down, neither seeking comfort, nor findinge any,
but in his agony traced from place to place, much like to Bacchus Nuns, or
to Cibeles braine-sicke Nymphs in Ida Mount he ran, resembling those whom
Driades and Faunes do force to fly. But when he saw himself busy bootles,
nothing to prevail, he satte him down, and entered straight to this
consultation.

Forget that pranked paramour pert, and let her go. Forget her Philotimus.
Nay, sooner shall the roaring froathie Seas ymatch the lofty Firmament in
height, and hellish Plutoes feltered den, with starbright heaven shall sooner
coupled be, and shining light with gloomye shades agree, and with the clear
dry day the drearie night conioyne, and smoking stifling scaldinge fire
convert to frostie ysicle snow, ere I forget, whom I have forgone, ah
dearest Aurelia.

And herewithall the tears ran down his cheeks apace. He was daily
troubled with this Quotidian, neither eating nor drinking, nor sleeping, but
fed I think with Aungells food, and by Gods imputation, dispensed for the time
from humaines usual conversation. He spent his time sometime studying how to
recover wealth to win his Lady again, sometimes composing Epitaphes for his
Tomb, thinking he could not long live, sometime in Meeters to praise his
Aurelia, on whom to think it did him good, and sometime in complaining the
frowardnes of his fates, among the rest these few that follow I thought good
to insert.

Who loses Love, and conquers care in lieu,
who pightes his pains, and pines for want of food,
His lossfull lot and crimeles curse I rue,
yet would he view my cause, his case were good.
His hap may be to fancy yet else where,
ah speme spent, my love and I am done.
Or he may drench and die in deep despair,
O that I might for bliss enjoy that boon.
Long have I served, and well deserud some meede,
yet do do I sterue with strife and sternefull nayes,
My constancy was causer of my creed,
that cruelty is cursed, that trust betraies.
A chearles case must needs cause chilling care,
O pale wanhope, when wanton wantes his wish
No dastard to be da^de where dole does dear,
as good to fast as feast where dearth's a dish.
What metal can resist the flaming fire?
no heart I think can hate those crystal eyes,
How can a bounden thrall retire desire?
The Eagles force subdues each bird that flies.
These rimes were made in great agony and anguish. But as every hill has his
dale, every tide his eb, and every tempeste his flawe of fair weather, so
had he some intermission of hi^ sobbinges, though he could not have remission
of all his sorrows. For thus he began to straighten his affections with
reasons rule. Though he were in disgrace with Aurelia, and defaced of all his
friends, yet God would either send remedy, or take him to his mercy. Though
his body nothing proportionable to his valor, were not big enough to beat his
foe Cornelius, yet did he see that the little dapper carcass was the tabernacle
of wit, and the louby bones a tipe of a dullard. Though in the ruin of his
riches he were brought to an exigent, and like to be exiled the precincts of
his country, yet did he reconsolate himself with his readinges and
experimentes, by which he found that Wit commonly wears a wallet at his back,
when Follies robes be veluets, and to this effect did he frame this petty
Pamphlet, whereof here I make illation.

When we have past the day in the Sea with perrill, the night of death does
take us in at the port of health. For who has a pattern or a lease of his
life, or what Obligation in this case may serve, without the performance of
many a condition? As often comes ihe lamb to the market as the elder sheep,
as often blastes the bloome as the riper fruit, and Gods joy in garlands, that
be fresh and green. Then let youth claim no prerogative, where no privilege
is granted, but wish and pray for the coming of his Christ, and watch and
ward that he come not unawares.

I have always thought that the guiltles prisoner with his clogged
conscience, lookinge for nothing but his fatal final sentence at the next gale
delivery, is not so subject to the summons of death, as we that are out of
circuit of such crimes, and free from the sentence of the bloody Judge. This
has ever been mine opinion, preferring the lingering of a certain death,
before ye lasting of an uncertain life.

And of all other, the sharpest wit (says Titleman) has the shortest life.
Because heat, which is the cause of quicknes, having pre-eminence in the
temperature of his body, does eat up the natural moisture which is a
sustenaunce to it, and so having nothing to feed on, burns up the carcass.
The matter of cold hail is thin and warm says Arist: warm water sooner
freezeth then cold lycoure says Velcurie. and I auouche that the hottest
constitution (which by the way, is most pregnant in wit) is the readiest
procurer of cold death. Soon ripe, soon rotten: quickly spent, that's easily
gotten: bauin burns brighte, but it is but a blaze: the flashinge lightening
is gone at a gaze: then this is my verdit. As those abortiui which are borne
before their time, never prove sightly men: so these forward youths (and too
forward says M. Askam) never prove old men.

If any man appose me in what sort of men I deem this passing work of wit,
for my cock, I would choose the little dapper Dick, take Robbin Hood who list,
let me have little John. Be not angry with me if I speak amiss. Aristotle is
my author, and will answer all replies: who making a bypartite division of
all kinds of men in his books of Policy, gives the burly boned bou^sers
(neither good for man nor woman, unless it be to lubber-leape them) the orders
of servitude, and to little timbred fellows (who want in weight, if you poise
them by bodies, but ready in wit, and quick as a Be) the government to rule,
the one appointing what to do, like Master Oiconomus, the goodman of the
house, the other taking aim at his masters mouth to execute his pleasure, So
that the masters: ^ye fattes the horse, though the Groom of the ^^^le give
him prouander.

The same Arist. assertes the most fools to be mos^e boulde and fierce.
Because as gross blood wherewith he aboundes, increases his strength, so it
must necessarily weaken the wit, and make a grossum caput. Contrariwise ye
tender blood, from whence thin rare spirits do breath (as our Philosophers
clepe them) enseebles the body, and kepes it down, whettes the wit and stunts
the stomach.

Folly aduauncing herself in that best book of Erasmus, his Encomion moriae,
and bragging her to be the mistress of al noble exploits, will admit none but
monsters into her muster: small men are scarce sufficient for a foot garrison
to watch the walls, not able to endure one nights cold, without a well
defencing shelter. She leuieth her army of huge boisterous hobs, well be^eming
for their understanders to be the ofspringe of Giauntes, who not only will
courageously forrige upon their enemies, but durst and would for their bigness
and folly, lay a second siedge to the hold of the Gods.

The politic Prince Agamemnon was of a middle pitche, and widly Ulysses of
somewhat less stature, whose words came forth like winter snow, such store he
had, as good Antenor describs him in Homer. Those therefore of hot composition,
and of mean rate in stature, liuelye, neat, and nimble, do, as Virgil
speaks of Bees in the fourth of his Georgickes, within that little corpse of
theirs, right noble stomachs bear.

For though they be not so rash and feareles as they of ye other sort, yet by
reading or reason, experience or policy, they dare in time do as much as
they, and for the others one matter well compassed with success, they will
bring ten thousand to happy end, if luck be aunswerable.

Lycurgus, not one clad with the stuntliest courage of all other, and far
beyond Aereithous in strength (I mean that Aereithous that bare the massy
club, wherewith he fighting got such praise, that he christened himself by
the name of Clubber) slew him tho by sleight, to whom he found himself
inferior in force, and Ereuthalion that mighty champion, was slain by good
foresight of the wi^e Nestor.

I have red that in an old smokie author, which the^ I thought worthy noting,
and here I mean to insert, and this it is in our vulgar tongue. I have seldom
seen a long man wise, or a low man lowly. Now this aspiring haughtines is
vsuallye joined with an excelling wit, whereof it proceeds. For having a sharp
capacity wherein he does most resemble the Gods, he desires to be seated in
some exalted throne, near to the Gods and therefore says one of Alexander, if
he had had a quantity of body, measured out to the quality of his mind, with
the one hand he had caught the East, and with the other he had raught the
West.

I mean not to make an Inuectiue against goodly corporal men, of whom for my
part I think very substancially, nor think not, but that as Aristotle says,
great heads, if they be not too great, have the best capacities, so great men,
if they be not monsters, have no want of wit. For Paulus Eginetus, I remember,
in his first book De medicina says, that a very little head is a certain
sign of a weak judgment, and want in quantity of brain: and I suppose,
that if their frame and match be even and equal, Nanes and Dwarfes must
needs be topped with such heads.

I can use no sharp aunsweres to excuse my self to these huge Polyphems,
neither have I any sound arguments to polishe the praises of such as be of ye
little reasonable sise: but this I can aledg drawn from Natural Philosophy,
yt the wittiest sconce has the greatest inclination to Venerie, wherewith
beginning to dallye too soon, though for a season it help the grouth, yet
does it prevent the natural grouth, and if Apolloes Physic be not wouen with
Apolloes wit, cuttes of the course of his years, before the fates have half
run their date, unless his peragons had the power of Dan Aurora, who
prolonged the youth of her friend Tithonus with supply of her moisture. Yet
this may be his comfort, that though he want Paris his personage, which is
common to many, he may have part of Achilles his prowess, which has
fellowship with few, and be endewed with Ulysses his wit, which I will not say,
is appropriate to himself.

The hills are not fertile, nor the valleys barren. The Sun in the highest
delights in the shadow which is shortest, and nourishes the Tree, whose
root grows deepest, not whose top springs loftiest.

Naythelesse, that seasonable air, and breeding up, and worthy race, may
quallifie a coward with courage, and portcolize ye pate with policy, Ajax
Telamon was wont to say, and I assent. And therefore those 9. worthies of the
Greeks, who at Hectors challenge to combat with any one single man, offered
themselves to wage battle, each of them severally, had not only braund
boisterous bodies, but well bumbast also with acute policy,

I dare not be too vehement against these champions, because as they be fools,
so commonly they be fortunate, whereas the other sort their co^riualls in the
former comparison, are God knows, more lofty then luckie. Which how it
comes to pass I know not, but that we see ragged walls have painted clothes,
when sound marble is naked: a crooked back must have a bumbast dublet, when a
straight body wears no such bolsteringes: that ill woods grow apace, when
good herbs sproute at ease: and that Nick Noddie has the luck, when
Welladay Wit lives in lack.

Bellerophon, whose shape, wit, and mind, were more meet for a demi God, then
for a mortlinge, whose semine race, and patrie breed, foreheld deaurate
scepters in Ephyra of Argos I Will, with how many forraies of enemies was he
afronted, and worse the^ any driuill assailed with azerd steel, to reaue his
life by stealth? What monsters had he ministered to be his combatantes? What
veins of lanes enforced to threede, but that God whom he implored to be his
gardaine, renforced him with armipotente and impugnable mart, to bring the
palm away, and prove them dastard parnels? He spending his young years with a
King in Graece ye hight Proetus, had caught (not cautele of it) in his love,
the Queen Andia, to whose disloialtie because he would not consent, she bare
her husband in hand, that he sought her dishonor, and besought him to reueng
it with austeritie of punishment. Proetus would not murder him in hugger
mugger in his own house, but forged letters of guile, wherewith he sent
Bellerophon to his Father in law King Rheon, the Lycian prince, with this
tenure, to reiourne the bearers return from time to time, and by some occasion
to put him to death. Rheon to give good enterteinment to his son in laws
entreatie, inioynes this Bellerophon to slay the dire monster Chimere, a
ghastfull thing, and for no man to do, as he supposde. The head and breast of
him were like a Lion, the middle like a goat, behind like a Dragon, and his
breathinges terrible flames: him, after much tiring toil, Bellerophon slew.
That done the Solymes down he hackt. Then the King appointed him to try with
many an Amazon: but still he was so steeld with hardy heart, that he laid the
life of these Amazons in morgage with Pluto, for his favor at such atttempts.
At length, to make a sure end of him, Rheon provided an ambushment of the
Lycians to set upon him hard by a fountains side, yet all this packed crew
Bellerophon murdered. With these dangers vndeseruedlye was noble Bellerophon
distress, though at length it pleased the Gods to innoble his innocence, and
the foresaid king to mount his credit.

This story of Bellerophon I thought meet to restore you, being once before
recited by Homer, because if Pegasus, the flying horse of Fame were alive
again, he could not be better busied, then to carry his renown through the
whole world* such store make I of it.

I could make you an inuentory of ten thousand more, that deserving well, were
meeded as ill, and fill a Pedlers pack with my rehearsalls, but this may
suffice for the drift of my declaration, and enough they say, is as good as a
feast.

And for the party opposite how well fools can fadge, I need but relate a
short alligation.

The cockscombe Phrixus is said to ride in the Sea upon a golden Ram: the
interpretation of which Embleame is, that he had all things ^t will that are
in the world. A doltishe Ass, and sibles stranger, enjoyed rich Phenops
wealth, the heritage of whose twain and only sonns, Thoon and Zanthus, was
intercepted by slaughter. Megeros the noddie had gathered an hutch full of
gold, when his elder brother a learned Phtlosopher, was urged to beg.

The compiling of this small volume, Philotimus thought some comfort to
himself, and would sometimes read it to help to rid his melancholye. But
now by Philotimus his favor, I must borrow a little leave to bestow on his
adversary Cornelius.

I will you to wit, that this Cornelius had been a long lover of one Laida, a
gallant courtly Gentlewoman, and one of Aureliaes fellows. This Laida (saving
Aurelia) was compere in heau- to any in the Court, and (saving brave Aurelia)
was fancied of Cornelius more then all other. On the other side, she by
disposition was very light, and therefore soon enamoured of his gracious
personage, covetous of coigne (as most women be) and therefore condiscended to
depose to all his interrogatories. Finally she see him more then her match in
any thing (except a little pelting wit) and therefore yielded to be his mate in
every thing, I except not bed pleasure.

This she did under guarde of his oath, which promised that in time convenient,
bridal banes should make amends for all: but when she see him started from
his hearts foredelight, and such a block as Aurelia laid to stumble at, that
never thought one straw would lie in her way, she set the hares head to the
goose giblings, and Spanyerdlike was as careless as he: marry she meant not to
hurt herself with keeping her choler close, but sent it wrapped in a scroull to
be an eyesore to him.

Laida to Cornelius.
Were ye so hot in my sacred service, that now you ar fled for holy religion?
Adieu sir Duns, a botch on your britch, God keep you from sickness, till sores
have consumed you.

When I got you, I gaind a flatterer, when I lost you, I f^^n a flincher, what
have I gaind, or what have I lost, judge you.

I know not whether is better to wail my good weal, that I received
unwillingly of a frantic foe, or smile at his sottishnes, embracing hardhap,
which gives him a serpent, and tells him its fish. Yet can I not choose but
weep, with an onion in mine eye, and an apple in my mouth, and better do I
think it to weep out mine eyes, never to see ye like caytiff again, then
laugh out my spene at his fickle folly, and hurt my self with extremetie of
passion.

Hey ho for Lucius, my mind is all on Fabian, Lysiteles is mine only joy,
Dinarchus want does make me moan. She is scarcely weather wise, that knows not
how usually the wind does chau^g, from East to West, from North to South: but
she is far less worldly wise, that stores not a choice for every change.

He that rides with one girth, may fear to be unhorsed, and she that feeds on
one friend, deserves to live with leauinges.

I grant by my folly I was inueigled with deceit, and hope that by patience,
I shall be comforted in distres.

The loss of hope abridgeth lamentation, and light belief has commonly
light love.

Thou art more meet for a widows joy, which lastes but a moment, then fit to
be a maidens phear, whose faith outlastes the heavens in durance.

I have been so undermined and countermined by thy overthwart ways, that
Theseus was not more glad of his deliuerye out of the Laborinth, then I reioise
to be freed of thy leasing forgeries. When my offense shall come to scanninge,
which has alienated thee so sodeinly from me, thou will be found as
fantastical as Nausicles a Merchant in Naucratia, which being in love with
Arsinoe, and often gratulated with her company, began in process to loath his
Arsinoe, because, when she sunge at his entreaty, her cheeks swelled, and her
eyes stared: or like ye Wife, which seeing one behave himself valiantlye in a
Tournement, fell in love with him, but when he put up his Beauer to take the
air, and the Woman coming apace to see him, perceived yt was her Husband,
she made a mock at the matter, and cared not for him.

Pray therefore for thy self, and so would I do for thee (although thou not
deserve it) but that the Gods would be offended to pray for so wicked a
perjured reprobate, that the reckoning of thy new hostess, be not rackt to a
more unreasonable rate, then was Aristippus his the Athenians, which by the
mischievous means of his second marriage was banished his country, and his
goodds confiscate. But like will to like, says the old proverb, a flinching
fool, to a fleeting flatterer, and this is true, and trusted of old, ye ever
a slouing, slim slam sibi quaerit.

I have been more liberal to thee of my maidenlye store, then now I am proud
on, and I fear thou art more prodigal in blabbing it out, then thou have
thank for: yet good beast, do not boast of thy shameful gettinge, for I gave
thee that, which then I had not, and thou receiuedst ye, which thou tookst not.

I know what I write, when I indite of thy knavery, and thou can level at my
meaning, by the aim of thy subteltye.

Surely there has happened a prodigious wonder in thy love: for whiles thou
louedst me, there was neither Winter, nor Summer, nor Spring, nor Harvest. Thou
did love me from midday till hye noone.

Yet I nothing marvel at it. For I never knew Capon yet love Hen: neither am
I ignorant, why your paramour is so passionate over you, she does it not I
warrant you, without consideration: for her ship being fraught, she may take a
passenger, and her belly being sped, take thee for advantage.

I see (Cornelius) that thou art one of those, that will run vii. miles to
kiss the stake a smock hung on, though thou haste more work at home, then
such a tinker as thou, can well botche

I was a threede too course for your spinning, for so you make semblaunce: yet
if your wheel had been steadfast and not casten the band, my web had been
fine inoughe for your slouenlye wear.

Mustard and pepper received into the stomach, hurt nothing at all, but being
applied to the outside of the skin, do blister and inflame. If any trespass I
have committed against thee, had come from inward malice, thou had been
excusable, but being so superficial, or not at all faulty, yt does quite
condemn thee.

Although the fixed stars should sooner fleet, then I would swear and
swerue, yet my reason being at liberty, teaches patience in adversity. The
same Jove which gives the Sun his splendent globe, has given the Moon, all
as he would, her horned head, yet as the Moon, by how much the more she is
distant from the Sun, by so much the brighter is illuminated: So, the
further I am dissociated from thee, the fitter shall I be to dissolve all
follies.

Farewell, and choke of it: for I never knew Rouer of any continuance, but at
length he rushed against the rocks, and so I trust will thou. And as Juno for
spite turning Parrhasis into a Bear, was the cause, that Jove for amends,
exalted her to be a neighbor star to the Northren poale: so the inckling of
this thy fact, will make my life exact, and esteemed among thy betters. I
commend me to thy cogginges, and salute thy ingratitude with an vnhartie
greeting.

Golden loookes are painted hooks. Beware.

Laida, once thine, and now her own.


These letters were as welcome to Cornelius, as a storm of wind to the month
of March. For this he looked and longed for, to be so lightly forsaken.
Immediately he resente an awnswere, which I imagine was of his writing, and
Aureliaes enditing. For when his apparel was of his back, all his wit was
dear of twopence.

Cornelius to Laida.
MY Lady, sweet Beauty, Sluts whelpe and her darlinge, I g^ete you well. I
received your letters the first day of my malice, dated the eightenth year of
the migne of a should.

When I had red thy ramping style, I feared thou were giddy, or in some
frantic ecstasy, and then I recald my thanckles fear, and hopt that thou
were even so indeeed.

Thou art like Menechmus Subreptus his wife, who thinking an other had been her
husband for their like resemblance, falsely burdened him with her husbands
knauerie: and I, because I am like my self, am slaunderouslye impeached of
inconstancy. As the bragging ostentation, of thy accusation, seems to
importe, I now am an other then I was before. For then I was reputed of
sufficient honesty, and now am descried of much cogging varletrie, so that my
good manners are grown out of fashion, and men's good opinion turned to
despair. If I am not as I was, as you say I am not, but straungely changed,
I cannot tell how, then praise Cornelius, whose credit is current, and blame me
no whit, for I am not the same.

Thy canckred rancour shows how far unfit thou art to have a loving spouse,
and thy hasty teatishnes, grounded only on suspicion, bewraies thy starting
fancy for every jealous freake.

Thy husband shall not need to be Justice of peace, for his wife will have a
charter to make her Justice of coram. If he punish others, and examine them of
wrongs, thou will school him, and ask him accountes. I was glad when I see
